  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_70f3c6f2-9b24-4d7f-89bd-f3e091f9a686'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10625315821098892507">The darklings will hunt once again.<br/><br/>The secret hour when time freezes arrives every night at midnight in Bixby, Oklahoma. It’s a dangerous time, when five teenagers are the only humans awake and dark creatures crawl out of the shadows, but at least the midnight hour is regular and predictable.<br/><br/>Until suddenly, the blue time comes ... in the middle of the day.<br/><br/>The noise of scho</span>
  <span id="freeText10625315821098892507" style="display:none">The darklings will hunt once again.<br /><br />The secret hour when time freezes arrives every night at midnight in Bixby, Oklahoma. It’s a dangerous time, when five teenagers are the only humans awake and dark creatures crawl out of the shadows, but at least the midnight hour is regular and predictable.<br /><br />Until suddenly, the blue time comes ... in the middle of the day.<br /><br />The noise of school stops. Cheerleaders are frozen in midair, teachers brought to a standstill. Everything is the haunted blue color of the midnight hour.<br /><br />The Midnighters can’t understand what’s happening, but as they scramble for answers, they discover that the walls between the secret hour and real time are crumbling. Soon the dark creatures will have a chance to feed after centuries of waiting, unless these five teenagers can find a way to stop them.<br /><br />A desperate race against time, a mind-blowing mystery of paranormal logic, a tale of ancient evil and spine-chilling sacrifice: blue noon is the exhilarating third volume in the Midnighters series by acclaimed author Scott Westerfeld.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer43478592" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2050544326119283349">Alright, I'm about to reveal the ending of this book.<br/>Go away if you haven't read the series or at least this book in the series!<br/><br/>Here we go, I'm about to give you an explanation to my likes and dislikes of the story!<br/><br/>Dislikes<br/>The book isn't just the ending to their journey, but also a beginning to a new journey.<br/>Jess is trapped in the blue time, frozen during the other twenty-four hours of the day, and she's the one who saved eveyone! Her sister and parents are left without her. Beth knows she's tra</span>
  <span id="freeText2050544326119283349" style="display:none">Alright, I'm about to reveal the ending of this book.<br />Go away if you haven't read the series or at least this book in the series!<br /><br />Here we go, I'm about to give you an explanation to my likes and dislikes of the story!<br /><br />Dislikes<br />The book isn't just the ending to their journey, but also a beginning to a new journey.<br />Jess is trapped in the blue time, frozen during the other twenty-four hours of the day, and she's the one who saved eveyone! Her sister and parents are left without her. Beth knows she's trapped and feels miserable without her. Her parents thinks she ran away and that's a horrible way to remember your child, as a runaway.<br />Johnathon is miserable without Jess all the time. He will also age much quicker than Jess and they can't be happy together because they know this. <br />Melissa and Rex are being seperated when they're the ones who keep each other mentally sane. Rex is stuck with a vegetable and a vegetable who is regaining her mind. Melissa will have to deal with more minds now than ever, even during the midnight hour.<br /><br />Likes<br />Dess is about to go into the world and introduce new Midnighters to Dessometrics. Also, she won't be a fifth wheel any longer and has plenty of guys to choose from.<br /><br />Finally, he didn't give a real ending. You can make up what you want to happen next. I have a few ideas...<br />1. Dess gets a boyfriend!<br />2. There will be a Midnighter with the ability to transports (like from America to Egypt!)<br />3. Once Maddy's mind heals, she'll take care of Rex's dad and he can rejoin Melissa.<br />4. There will be a Midnighter who can make people that are not born at midnight Midnighters, reuniting Jess and Beth.<br />5. (My favorite) There will be a new midnighter that can release Jess from her prison of being trapped in the midnight hour, or can trap Johnathon in it so they can be together.<br />6. I've also thought of the idea (and I don't like it) but there's the possiblity that Johnathon may age and find someone else to love since Jess is trapped in the midnight hour.<br />7. Dess finally figures out the midnight hour and is able to release Jess, or trap Johnathon with her.<br />8. After Johnathon and the others are gone, Jess (still stuck in the midnight hour) may commit suicide.<br />9.After Johnathon and the others are gone, Jess (still stuck in the midnight hour)will lead all future Midnighters.<br />10. Rex will finally snap and turn into a creature and Melissa might have to put him down, causing herself to commit suicide.<br /><br />Well, I won't go on any further, even though I have a few other millon ideas. But it is great to wonder about all the other characters that are going to come into play! Also I love the idea of getting to choose the way I want the story to end up. He could've wrote a fourth, and I would so read it, but he didn't. He left the rest to our imagination, and I like the idea of that. Though I do wish I knew what he wanted to happen in the future for the characters, it's obvious that Dess will have her happy ending, but what about the other four? One more thing, he put alot of time and effort into this series, and I liked it, alot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2050544326119283349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2067038970360441989">Read more reviews <a href='http://pepperinkbooks.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>I guess that this book's biggest flaw is that its just a replay from the two others. By that I mean that the Midnighters search, go out and investigate, live their normal life, fight the Darklings until they realize they need to stop the big problem blocking their way. Surprise, this time they really need to save the world.<br/><br/>I honestly wanted to be done with this book. It dragged too long and because the story played out always in the same place, as in Bixby and its surround</span>
  <span id="freeText2067038970360441989" style="display:none">Read more reviews <a href="http://pepperinkbooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />I guess that this book's biggest flaw is that its just a replay from the two others. By that I mean that the Midnighters search, go out and investigate, live their normal life, fight the Darklings until they realize they need to stop the big problem blocking their way. Surprise, this time they really need to save the world.<br /><br />I honestly wanted to be done with this book. It dragged too long and because the story played out always in the same place, as in Bixby and its surroundings (well, in this book the Midnighters actually go to another town, but it's still near Bixby), most of the things were predictable.<br /><br />Jessica and Johnathan were uninteresting. Their relationship didn't have any spice, it was just too plain. Rex, on the other side, became my favorite character. I like how he is one of the only Midnighters that actually evolved through out the book. Melissa, too, became less of a prick, and Dess got over her brooding.<br /><br />The plot was well developed, interesting, very connected to our present society and humanity's sins and clearly sending out its message but not laid out well enough as I mentioned before. If only Westerfield could have gone a bit out of the box, just a little bit, given a fresher taste, than I might have enjoyed this final book. Even if the description, fights and action are well written, it dragged too much.<br /><br />The ending could have had such a bigger impact if it had also been handled properly. Many disliked the ending, which I fear I will not reveal, because it really shut things up. I liked it. It was dramatic, cruel, at my taste, but it didn't affect me as much as such endings usually do. When you read the book, and if you've already read it, maybe you'll get what i mean.<br /><br />In conclusion, a somewhat poorly executed serie final, in my opinion. Repetitive and dragging. It is worth reading if you want to know how the serie ends, though, and if you want to see a badass Rex.<br /></span>

<div id="review_16318225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16318225" />
    <a title="Eshusdaughter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/742623-eshusdaughter"><img alt="Eshusdaughter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505110197p2/742623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16318225?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eshusdaughter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eshusdaughter" href="/user/show/742623-eshusdaughter">Eshusdaughter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16318225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11438403172472386285">In the final book of the Midnighter's trilogy, the blue time is beginning to fracture and fall apart. The five Midnighters, Dess, Jonathan, Jessica, Melissa and Rex are left scrambling, trying to find out why and prevent the entire world from becoming one big darkling buffet. <br/><br/>Like the other books this one is action-packed and rapid-paced from the first word to the last. We discover more about the lore and about the old Midnighter culture in Bixby. I loved the character development that has happe</span>
  <span id="freeText11438403172472386285" style="display:none">In the final book of the Midnighter's trilogy, the blue time is beginning to fracture and fall apart. The five Midnighters, Dess, Jonathan, Jessica, Melissa and Rex are left scrambling, trying to find out why and prevent the entire world from becoming one big darkling buffet. <br /><br />Like the other books this one is action-packed and rapid-paced from the first word to the last. We discover more about the lore and about the old Midnighter culture in Bixby. I loved the character development that has happened throughout the series and especially in this last book. While the series began with Jessica, the subsequent books made the other characters just as central to the story. It was an engaging read and one I'm sorry is over. It was so hard to put this book down and pace myself as I read! <br /><br />SPOILER WARNING - DON'T READ BELOW IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE BOOK<br /><br />Despite how much I liked the book, however. I'm a little disatisfied with the ending. That's why you only see four stars on this review. Jessica stuck in the blue time just doesn't feel right. The book even points out how quickly Jonathan and Jessica's relationship will get squicky and you're just left feeling bad for Jonathan and also for Jessica's family. I don't expect all my books to end with a perfect happy ending but this one just felt wrong - I didn't see the inevitability of it. There are so many other ways it could have gone. Also, the last line, while amusing, didn't fit the series either. We end with Dess when we began with Jessica. I think the series should have ended with a sentence about Jessica as well. Saying it's cool to be the one who does the math just feels flip when the book could have ended on better line. Westerfeld nailed the endings in all four of his Uglies series books so that's why I'm critical of this one. Other than that quibbling though I adored this book and the others. They were fun reads - nothing that was earth shattering but fun and fast. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11438403172472386285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7128762499594747603">Third and presumably final book of Midnighters. Not one of Westerfeld's better books or better series. This one in particular felt rushed that it did have a true actual ending. The characters kept on making annoying choices rather than interesting or smart choices. <div id="review_2206008423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2206008423" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206008423?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8204165-blue-noon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=high-school-days">high-school-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206008423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8789766040614070424">A bittersweet ending to this unique trilogy. <br/><br/>Having gotten used to their secret hour, the Midnighters are thrown for a loop when the blue hour arrives during the day. Soon their fears are realized when they figure out that the rip between worlds is failing, and there may be no way to stop it and keep the monsters out.<br/><br/>I liked the flow of this one. New elements were thrown in that threw our crew for a loop and it was fun to watch them try to figure out what was going on. But we also got to see the</span>
  <span id="freeText8789766040614070424" style="display:none">A bittersweet ending to this unique trilogy. <br /><br />Having gotten used to their secret hour, the Midnighters are thrown for a loop when the blue hour arrives during the day. Soon their fears are realized when they figure out that the rip between worlds is failing, and there may be no way to stop it and keep the monsters out.<br /><br />I liked the flow of this one. New elements were thrown in that threw our crew for a loop and it was fun to watch them try to figure out what was going on. But we also got to see the strain that this secret life was taking on them personally. Home lives were falling apart and even their own friendships were straining. <br /><br />Sadly though, I never really connected with any of the characters. I'm not sure why. I just never felt any sense of "OMG NO" when bad things happened. I didn't swoon when characters made a love connection. I just didn't feel it. <br /><br />Also, why didn't Jessica's sister get taken by the monsters? Because she was such a little shit. And speaking of her sister, I did feel that the ending was a little too sweet on their part, but again, that may just be me not connecting. <br /><br />Overall, an interesting series to read, but not sure it will be one I remember. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8789766040614070424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_58853294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58853294" />
    <a title="Angi M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109873-angi-m"><img alt="Angi M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190904411p2/109873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58853294?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angi M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angi M" href="/user/show/109873-angi-m">Angi M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109873-angi-m?shelf=fantasyadventure">fantasyadventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58853294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2688675313585080360">I love this series, love the characters, but I have to say the ending totally sucks! Mr. Westerfeld blew it. It sounds like he got to a point where he was just sick of writing, sick of the story and wanted to move on to other things so he went to someone who had never read the stories, gave that person a quick recap and then asked how it should end and he said 'Ok, that'll do' and just walked away from it. The ending doesn't make any sense! It's like he never even met any of the characters befor</span>
  <span id="freeText2688675313585080360" style="display:none">I love this series, love the characters, but I have to say the ending totally sucks! Mr. Westerfeld blew it. It sounds like he got to a point where he was just sick of writing, sick of the story and wanted to move on to other things so he went to someone who had never read the stories, gave that person a quick recap and then asked how it should end and he said 'Ok, that'll do' and just walked away from it. The ending doesn't make any sense! It's like he never even met any of the characters before! Jonathan &amp; Rex &amp; Melissa would never make the decisions he has them making at the end. It would never happen because it wouldn't put them any closer to getting what they want. Which is disappointing because right up until the very last chapter this book was excellent! Perfect.<br />I read on Westerfeld's website that Dess was his favorite character and it kinda seems like he just blew her off for most of this book (she didn't even get to do much of anything at all in the final showdown)and then he felt bad about it so he threw the rest of the characters to the wolves and let Dess give herself a smug pat on the back. Which is completely useless.<br />SO, here's what you should do. Read the series, because they really are great, and then when you get to the last chapter of Blue Noon, either write your own ending (because it HAS to be better than Westerfeld's) OR assume that the very next morning Rex wakes up and says<br />'Ok, guys, change of plans. What we were going to do yesterday would only be frustrating and fruitless and it was a stupid idea anyway. I'm the leader of this group and we still have 2 more years of High School so here's what we'll do: Jonathan, you work on solving Jessica's problem or, if you get the chance, just become like her. Melissa, you help me w/ my halfling problem while using the contortion to mindcast for other new midnighters. We'll contact them, spill the beans, give tips. We'll have a chat w/ Jessica's family...'. When Maddy says 'The Bixby of my day was blah, blah, blah' He'd say 'Well, it's not your day anymore. It's ours and Bixby is now an oasis for midnighters everywhere'. Dess would bide her time becoming famous as the best anti-darkling defense weapons developer in the world until she got out of High School and then she'd go show off her big brain in college and the story could still end on her smug one-liner. Bada-bing bada-boom! Much better than the real ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2688675313585080360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41291533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41291533" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1709422-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416431345p2/1709422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41291533?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/1709422-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709422-jean?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41291533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2777637197434352900">Wow, <i>Midnighters</i> ended with a bang; quite an apocolyptic wrap-up for the series. Perhaps I should have expected this, having read the <i>Uglies</i> series, but I guess it just seemed like such a <i>contained</i> story in the first book that it caught me by surprise to see things get so... big in this one.<br/><br/>Well, it was definitely action-packed and suspenseful. My favorite part of the book was watching Rex develop--he became by far the most interesting character in the whole story as he dealt with both his inter</span>
  <span id="freeText2777637197434352900" style="display:none">Wow, <i>Midnighters</i> ended with a bang; quite an apocolyptic wrap-up for the series. Perhaps I should have expected this, having read the <i>Uglies</i> series, but I guess it just seemed like such a <i>contained</i> story in the first book that it caught me by surprise to see things get so... big in this one.<br /><br />Well, it was definitely action-packed and suspenseful. My favorite part of the book was watching Rex develop--he became by far the most interesting character in the whole story as he dealt with both his internal changes and grappled with history. Here Westerfeld was at his best: he had his characters learn how to question what they'd read and been taught, but he never became particularly preachy to his reader about that lesson. <br /><br />It wasn't a perfect experience for me. He still overused certain phrases and didn't seem to always think through all the details and characterizations. A couple times I found myself confused over why a character would say one thing in one chapter when the chapter before they'd expressed the opposite view. I still don't feel like he had a good grasp of the locale.<br /><br />On the other hand, Westerfeld certainly has a knack for telling a compelling and creative story. I found <i>Midnighters</i> to be superior to <i>Uglies</i> in those respects: while the premise of <i>Uglies</i> was original, his actual plotlines became very repetitive and his characters were much flatter. I had to grow to like the midnighters, but eventually I did (well, except Jonathan...) and I always felt like the story was going somehere new and unexpected. I have to hand it to Westerfeld: he doesn't back away from a bittersweet ending, but I think it was a strong ending, just open-ended enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2777637197434352900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82452934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82452934" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82452934?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82452934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9728858456974412870"><i>Blue Noon</i> is the third and final installment of the Midnighter's trilogy. In this book the five teenagers that experience the secret hour begin to question everything they've believed in about Bixby's history as the town's secret hour and real time start to mesh together. As Halloween draws closer each Midnighter begins to fully feel the darklings anticipation to feast, and they have to band together one last time in order to protect all the innocent people who inhabit Bixby, Oklahoma from a tot</span>
  <span id="freeText9728858456974412870" style="display:none"><i>Blue Noon</i> is the third and final installment of the Midnighter's trilogy. In this book the five teenagers that experience the secret hour begin to question everything they've believed in about Bixby's history as the town's secret hour and real time start to mesh together. As Halloween draws closer each Midnighter begins to fully feel the darklings anticipation to feast, and they have to band together one last time in order to protect all the innocent people who inhabit Bixby, Oklahoma from a total midnight slaughter.<br /><br />Overall, Westerfeld has crafted an amazing finale for a great series with <i>Blue Noon</i>. He doesn't stop the fast-paced action and sudden realizations that all the characters share in this novel. In more ways than one <i>Blue Noon</i> connects with its predecessors by having great action sequences, character relationships, and interesting storyline.<br /><br />The one thing I didn't find particularly to my taste in <i>Blue Noon</i> was the ending. The ending itself was fine, if not bittersweet and a bit apocalyptic. The thing I didn't like so much was that throughout the first 2/3 of the story he made readers anticipate one moment or battle (if you've read the book you know what I'm taking about) and during that one moment or battle it felt really rushed and a bit disorganized. So that was a bit of a let-down.<br /><br />However, <i>Blue Noon</i> will still satisfy the science-fiction fans out there who have read the previous two installments, without a doubt. This was a satisfying series by Westerfeld and even though personally I'm not a fan of sci-fi his work here was good and made me read the entire trilogy - something that normally I never would have done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9728858456974412870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2753319588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2753319588" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45269487-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588862675p2/45269487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2753319588?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/45269487-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2753319588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2130022581247044899">I’m kind of glad this didn’t have a total happily-ever-after. <br/>This series’ concept is so cool and different, I loved it. <br/>I particularly liked Dess, the polymath. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_345927919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345927919" />
    <a title="Jacki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/306690-jacki"><img alt="Jacki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366077657p2/306690.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345927919?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacki" href="/user/show/306690-jacki">Jacki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060519575" href="/book/show/959336.Blue_Noon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/306690-jacki?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345927919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17821451429460665465">I feel satisfied with this ending. Westerfeld's story idea was a good one--full of fantasy and horror and intrigue. His execution might not have been the best, but I was sold on the fantasy of it. There were a few things that bothered me with this novel--all of which were things that bothered me consistently with the others in this trilogy. But in the end, I felt good about it. <br/><br/>Here are a few things that bothered me:<br/>The more I tried to think logically about what was happening, the more I saw hol</span>
  <span id="freeText17821451429460665465" style="display:none">I feel satisfied with this ending. Westerfeld's story idea was a good one--full of fantasy and horror and intrigue. His execution might not have been the best, but I was sold on the fantasy of it. There were a few things that bothered me with this novel--all of which were things that bothered me consistently with the others in this trilogy. But in the end, I felt good about it. <br /><br />Here are a few things that bothered me:<br />The more I tried to think logically about what was happening, the more I saw holes in his plot. I pointed out in the last book that using latitude and longitude didn't make sense considering that the beginning of this mythology took place before those lines were understood by the local people. In the same way, hours, and calendars would be useless. <br /><br />Forgetting the complications of using hours and minutes, let's talk about calendars. He points out, somewhere in an earlier book and even in this one that there are differences in calendars used over the years. There's a comment about when months were in a different order. But there are a few holes in all of this. The months we work with today are from the Georgian calendar, put into effect by Pope George the who-knows-which-number. Not only is it relatively new in creation, but it's special in that it's a solar calendar instead of a lunar one. This means that it follows the sun and seasons instead of the moon. Solar and lunar calendars function very differently. For more details ask a Muslim, Jew, or pretty much anyone from Asia. They all use lunar calendars. The Georgian calendar was introduced to the Americas by European colonists. <br /><br />I'm willing to bet a large sum of money (though I have not researched this myself) that before Europeans came to America, any calendar the natives were using was not solar, but lunar. The Mayan calendar is a lunar one. This means that Samhain would not fall on the same day each year--none of the months would be exactly the same each year--they're all dependent on the moon. <br /><br />Take the same basic concept of where our hours, minutes, and day changes come from and you've got the other plot hole that I found. (Who the hell decided that our day should change in the middle of the night, anyway?)<br /><br />Now, I realize that's a whole lot of issue with the story. I wish he would have done a little bit more research on these things and covered himself a little better. But I still enjoyed the story. I like his spread of characters, his change in perspective in each chapter, his build up to the climax, and most importantly, I loved how he brought it to a close. <br /><br />Endings can be very tricky. Especially in trilogies like this. I feel that Suzanne Collins failed us in her ending to the Hunger Games trilogy because she just dropped our emotions and anticipation without care and wrapped things up too quickly. Westerfeld didn't do that. He surprised us with an extra little twist on the ending, pushed the characters into their own futures, and then released the reader with something that makes us feel sad that it's over, but encourages our imagination to keep on rolling with the story. I like that tactic. It's satisfying enough to know there wont be another book, but it's open enough to not let the story die at the end of the page. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17821451429460665465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136511942" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=last-book-of-series">last-book-of-series</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer136511942&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136511942" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8040605637408835834">Plot Summary: When time freezes in the middle of the day, during a school pep rally, the Midnighters have a problem. The secret hour is slowly making its way into the real world. The last book in the midnighters trilogy is all about the adventure of trying to keep the secret hour in the secret hour.<br/><br/>The Midnighters begin to experience the secret hour more and more frequently during daylight hours. To make matters worse, Rex's darkling side cannot always control itself, and may be becoming stronge</span>
  <span id="freeText8040605637408835834" style="display:none">Plot Summary: When time freezes in the middle of the day, during a school pep rally, the Midnighters have a problem. The secret hour is slowly making its way into the real world. The last book in the midnighters trilogy is all about the adventure of trying to keep the secret hour in the secret hour.<br /><br />The Midnighters begin to experience the secret hour more and more frequently during daylight hours. To make matters worse, Rex's darkling side cannot always control itself, and may be becoming stronger. By using Madeline and other resources, the Midnighters find out that on the night of Samhain (Halloween), the Secret Hour will expand, and more of the Earth will be sucked up.<br /><br />This is because there is a "rip" in true midnight, which allows non-midnighters to slip into the blue time, that is expanding like a seam in fabric. While trying to keep people out of these dangerous zones, Jessica has some trouble with her curious little sister Beth. True midnight (usually confined to the secret hour) will last for the whole day, and all humans and creatures within it will be awake, no longer 'stiff'.<br /><br />This will allow the darklings to feast once again upon the creatures of day-unless the five teens find a way to stop it from happening. When Jessica and her boyfriend Johnathan, manage to stop the "blue time" from spreading to the whole world, Jessica unfortunately gets sucked into the "blue time". <br /><br />To Johnathan and the whole Midnighter's teams dismay, she will forever be trapped in the blue time, only able to live for an hour of every day. Jessica's parents become very sad about their daughter's<br />"disappearance" and are still greiving about her loss when Beth comes to visit Jess for the last time. Both sisters share an emotional time with each other before Johnathan has his moment to say good bye. Finally, with a half hour to spare, Johnathan takes Jessica and Beth on their last flight through the blue time.<br /><br />Thoughts:<br />First time readers to this series MUST start from book one. If you don't you will lose some much needed background information on the 5 midnighters themselves.<br /><br />I still don't much care Melissa's character, but at least in this one she became a guiding force instead of a nag.<br /><br />I'm not shocked that Jessica sacrificed herself and is now in what is called Temporal Dependence. Ever since Madeline said that she manipulated her into coming to Bixby, I figured she would be either the villian in the end, or the hero. <br /><br />Cassie, Beth and Angie Grayfoot all play pivotal parts in this last book. Beth, more of a bad part than a good part. I would have strangled Beth had she been my sister, but that's neither here nor there at this point. What's done is done, and the series is finished.<br /><br />Could there be any chance that another spin-off of this series would be worth the read? Especially knowing that three of the main characters are going away from Bixby searching for other Midnighters. <br /><br />Finis - Overall rating 3.5 stars. There wasn't enough of Dess in this story, and sometimes I just wanted to scream at Jessica for being so silly. <br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer36457024" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18081566540505996710">Um...okay. Way to ruin the last book of an amazing series that had lots of potential, Scott. Thanks a lot.<br/><br/>The other two books were soooo good, crazily astounding. And most of this book was, too. Up until the last chapter, it had all the good stuff that comes with the Midnighters trilogy; action and suspense and excitement and thrill and eye-glue and heart-speed and all the rest of the kit and kaboodle.   <span id="freeText18081566540505996710" style="display:none">Um...okay. Way to ruin the last book of an amazing series that had lots of potential, Scott. Thanks a lot.<br /><br />The other two books were soooo good, crazily astounding. And most of this book was, too. Up until the last chapter, it had all the good stuff that comes with the Midnighters trilogy; action and suspense and excitement and thrill and eye-glue and heart-speed and all the rest of the kit and kaboodle. I was really happy with it and thought it was sooooo good...until the ending.<br /><br />The ending completely killed it.<br /><br />The only words I can come up with to describe it are, “What the <i>HELL</i>?!?”<br /><br />It was really sad, bad, horrible, weird and confusing, not to mention the fact that it didn't make a lot of sense. Uh, okay...Jessica gets swallowed up by the blue time and can only live during midnight (how does that work?). For some reason Melissa and Jonathan are leaving Bixby and going to travel the world to find other Midnighters, since the blue time has somehow swallowed the whole world (and somehow Jessica is going to be able to go with them, even though she doesn't exist during the daylight hours). Rex and Dess get completely excluded and left out to rot away in Bixby (???@??@??@??!!?!?!?!). And Jessica's parents are left sobbing their eyes out, no clue what is going on, and are considering moving somewhere else, waiting until they get “more evidence” (of what? Scott didn't care to explain what the blazes he was rambling about. If it's “more evidence” of whether Jessica's alive or not, would you care to tell us?). Oh yeah, and the creepy fact that Jessica is going to be nineteen when Jonathan is going to be a vegetable of eighty years old. <br /><br />Gee, thanks.<br /><br />It might not have been so bad if Scott had written it better. Like, actually explaining things better, in a much less confusing way, and maybe not leaving a bunch of information out. And maybe not bringing up random, shocking statements and then not clarifying them. Plus the whole time gap thing; it was quite annoying when Scott kept skipping huge gaps of time throughout the books, especially at the end, and making us do the work of filling in the gaps.<br /><br />Ugh. Talk about killing a good series.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong- the rest of the book was still AMAZING. It was just the ending that ticked me off. I only took one star off for that. XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="18081566540505996710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer459089316725575035">I'm not going to be redundant here, because everything I could say about this book is all the same stuff I've said in the first two. So I'll just talk about the ending.<br/><br/>I think I may have liked it, in some dark and twisted way. Jessica had to touch this lightning bolt in the blue time, and with her powers it would come back to life closing the rift that was bleeding normal time with blue time. She just obviously wasn't sure about what would happen when she touched it. But she did (duh) and she en</span>
  <span id="freeText459089316725575035" style="display:none">I'm not going to be redundant here, because everything I could say about this book is all the same stuff I've said in the first two. So I'll just talk about the ending.<br /><br />I think I may have liked it, in some dark and twisted way. Jessica had to touch this lightning bolt in the blue time, and with her powers it would come back to life closing the rift that was bleeding normal time with blue time. She just obviously wasn't sure about what would happen when she touched it. But she did (duh) and she ends up getting stuck in the midnight hour for all eternity. The end.<br /><br />It's sad and depressing, but I think it actually gives weight to the characters I've never been very interested in. As Jonathan realized that when he would be dying of old age and Jessica (only living for one hour every day) would just be in her twenties or so, well I actually felt his sadness. And just how all the midnighters seemed to be going their own way coupled with the realization that Jess' parents would never know what happened to her really added to the unhappiness of it all.<br /><br />Also of note is Beth in this book. She gets a much more upfront role, finally finding out about the midnighters and their secret lives. Her final flight with Jon and Jessica was quite nice, too.<br /><br />I will say this once more, though: this series is not BAD by any means. It has a truly original premise and some great mythology. I can totally see why people enjoy them. It just never hit home with me.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_475737772" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475737772" />
    <a title="Emma Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15399188-emma-lauren"><img alt="Emma Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370399132p2/15399188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475737772?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Lauren" href="/user/show/15399188-emma-lauren">Emma Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475737772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14174223141267756529">Blue Noon by Scott Westerfeld was the third and final installment in the Midnighters Trilogy, and frankly, was boring. I could have lived without the entire first two hundred pages of the book, and just went into the main storyline. And the side plots about Rex becoming more darkling than human, and Melissa becoming a better mindcaster, were utterly worthless. I mean, if you want to do some character development, at least have the development lead to something.. The most interesting character in</span>
  <span id="freeText14174223141267756529" style="display:none">Blue Noon by Scott Westerfeld was the third and final installment in the Midnighters Trilogy, and frankly, was boring. I could have lived without the entire first two hundred pages of the book, and just went into the main storyline. And the side plots about Rex becoming more darkling than human, and Melissa becoming a better mindcaster, were utterly worthless. I mean, if you want to do some character development, at least have the development lead to something.. The most interesting character in this entire book is Jonathon, but we almost never hear from him, and his relationship with Jessica is almost always glossed over entirely. I wanted to feel emotional about the ending, but it is impossible when you cannot connect to any of these characters. And the epilogue.... not the whole book, just the epilogue, was just awful. I've never had a book wth a decent ending have such an awful epilogue before. Why would the book end with Dess talking? That makes no sense. And worst of all, she is talking about careers that she wants to go into once she leaves Bixby. This isn't the end of an inspirational high school film, it's a sci-fi drama, where people have literally been brutally murdered, and NO ONE is doing anything! Ugh. This had such potential to be great, and I'm really disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14174223141267756529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061954665" href="/book/show/10160762-blue-noon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14645683-enzo?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14645683-enzo?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14645683-enzo?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1202903027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13026555400535124129">So I am able to put another great series by Scott Westerfeld down. The Midnighters series is really fun and its last volume is really fun, filled with action and even more Blue time which is the best part of the novels. <br/>We see our heroes almost beaten in the previous novel now fighting for their lives. Each Midnighter gets to that point were they start thinking they will lose but its by acting as a team that they have prevailed in the past. But will that hold true this time around? When even mor</span>
  <span id="freeText13026555400535124129" style="display:none">So I am able to put another great series by Scott Westerfeld down. The Midnighters series is really fun and its last volume is really fun, filled with action and even more Blue time which is the best part of the novels. <br />We see our heroes almost beaten in the previous novel now fighting for their lives. Each Midnighter gets to that point were they start thinking they will lose but its by acting as a team that they have prevailed in the past. But will that hold true this time around? When even more is at stake. Rex was really hurt and seems in no condition to take on even more of the Darklings. Will the humans helping the Darklings come back and finish the job they started? Can they rely on each other after Melissa's betrayal? <br />So many questions and even more pile up as Westerfeld weaves his magic in this novel. He gives and teases, he pulls and straightens all to keep the reader on edge. Good job overall and one that you will appreciate after reading a fun series one that never takes itself to seriously to forget it has to entertain and keep us guessing.<br />Well worth the read. I can see how this series one of Westerfeld earlier works was a good jumping point towards Leviathan. Don't miss out pickup the MIdnighters!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13026555400535124129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19233638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19233638" />
    <a title="Echo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/851657-echo"><img alt="Echo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201652181p2/851657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19233638?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Echo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Echo" href="/user/show/851657-echo">Echo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/851657-echo?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/851657-echo?shelf=ya-supernatural">ya-supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19233638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2821481063117467681">What a gripping ending for a fantastic series! This book continued to surprise me with how much more can happen within this make-believe world the author has dreamed up. None of these books has been a re-hash of what happened or even made you feel like you were stuck in a loop that started way back when. I think each of the books could actually stand on its own as a gripping story, but is easier to really get deeply into as you read all of them. <br/><br/>I kind of hated the ending, but it was a very perf</span>
  <span id="freeText2821481063117467681" style="display:none">What a gripping ending for a fantastic series! This book continued to surprise me with how much more can happen within this make-believe world the author has dreamed up. None of these books has been a re-hash of what happened or even made you feel like you were stuck in a loop that started way back when. I think each of the books could actually stand on its own as a gripping story, but is easier to really get deeply into as you read all of them. <br /><br />I kind of hated the ending, but it was a very perfect adolescent ending. I loved where Rex went with everything that happened to him &amp; the way he was able to overcome. I was surprised because I started out with Dess being one of my favorite characters, but she just kind of lost momentum for me &amp; Rex took over as the one I kept wanting to know more about. I know Jessica &amp; Johnathon are supposed to be the "main" characters in this book, but they're story really took a back seat for me to everything else that was going on.<br /><br />I loved when the Darklings spoke to the Midnighters &amp; the description of their minds. It was very creepy &amp; believable. I'm excited to read more by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2821481063117467681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_37425114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37425114" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1698392-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232266732p2/1698392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37425114?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/1698392-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">To those who want to see what happens in the series :)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1698392-jill?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1698392-jill?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37425114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17241016790833009206">OK, I hate to admit it, but this series got a little boring to me. I really enjoyed the first book because I thought it was a really cool idea, the second was still pretty good, and then the third book got a little slow -- but I had to see how it ended, so I finished it. The author didn't give it a definite ending, so if he writes another book I'm bound to read it too, just because I'm really concerned about a couple of the characters. <br/><br/>The author didn't totally make me LOVE the characters, but I</span>
  <span id="freeText17241016790833009206" style="display:none">OK, I hate to admit it, but this series got a little boring to me. I really enjoyed the first book because I thought it was a really cool idea, the second was still pretty good, and then the third book got a little slow -- but I had to see how it ended, so I finished it. The author didn't give it a definite ending, so if he writes another book I'm bound to read it too, just because I'm really concerned about a couple of the characters. <br /><br />The author didn't totally make me LOVE the characters, but I liked them on a superficial level. The points of view kept changing with every chapter, so you didn't totally get extremely personal with just one person, which is what I prefer. Also, the idea that was cool that I liked from the beginning, got a little old for me. It's still a cool idea, but the author did every possible thing he could with it, and it just got a little old. I still like the author, but it's just not going to be something I give rave reviews about, just a pretty good book to pass the time. Anyway, sorry to disappoint, but maybe you'll like it a little more than me -- I'll be curious to see what other people think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17241016790833009206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430291026?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily" href="/user/show/13470820-lily">Lily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430291026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8461546264494091163">I wasn't impressed with this book. I loved the first book when I read it years back, and I still thought it was pretty good when I read it again a few weeks ago. The idea of a "secret hour" is fascinating and I couldn't wait to read more about it, but this book... Well, it has it's interesting moments, I'll give it that, but overall, I found it rather boring and I ended up skimming through a lot of it just so I could quickly finish the series.<br/><br/>But, ugh, the ending... The ending sucked. I wasn't s</span>
  <span id="freeText8461546264494091163" style="display:none">I wasn't impressed with this book. I loved the first book when I read it years back, and I still thought it was pretty good when I read it again a few weeks ago. The idea of a "secret hour" is fascinating and I couldn't wait to read more about it, but this book... Well, it has it's interesting moments, I'll give it that, but overall, I found it rather boring and I ended up skimming through a lot of it just so I could quickly finish the series.<br /><br />But, ugh, the ending... The ending sucked. I wasn't satisfied with it at all. It left me feeling disappointed. Disappointed with the book, with the series, with the characters. <br /><br />I sort of wish I had just stopped reading the series after the first book--not that the second book was horrible. I read it a few weeks ago, the day after I reread the first one. It was good, but the first one is still my favorite of the three. <br /><br />I'd recommend this series to young adults though. I'm sure others will love them all even though <i>I</i> don't particularly like this last book. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FphU/zByYbyd7W2Dpt1ZQxUWlm6FSuKwRueIJBMvNeH2ts44oK3qB2M5cTIijdv4c3CsNNgWxMJC9HAPSUtErQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BRCtPkAGpMcfht7tWhuGiwMDOqA3u8WucrqkheNEbC3lPjf50NkvfOFSwlzeSwQwZWUA+mrn49x2qVyuuSAdYQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15138058116630012177">Scott Westerfeld is a New York Times bestselling author of YA. He was born in the Texas and now lives in Sydney and New York City. In 2001, Westerfeld married fellow author Justine Larbalestier.<br/><br/>He is best known for the Uglies and Leviathan series. His next book, IMPOSTORS, returns to the world of Uglies. It comes out September 11, 2018.</span>
